Divine Decree
intermediate
8 min
Kasb and Refutation of Jabr
Sanusi defines kasb and refutes Jabr in one continuous argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari concept of kasb (acquisition) and why Sanusi declares the Jabri position a bid'a.

Core Idea
Kasb preserves human responsibility while affirming Allah's sole creative power.

In this short but dense passage, Sanusi defines the key term 'kasb' and immediately uses it to refute the fatalist doctrine of Jabr. The passage is foundational for understanding the Ash'ari position on human agency: humans acquire actions without creating them, and this acquisition is what makes moral accountability meaningful. Let's unpack it step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Start by reading the Arabic text once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the flow: definition, purpose, then refutation.
The Arabic is concise; notice the particle 'fa' (thus) marking the conclusion.
2
Identify the definition of kasb
Look for how Sanusi describes the relationship between created power (al-qudra al-ḥāditha) and the action (al-maqdūr): it is 'concomitant without effect'. This is the core of kasb.
3
Understand the role of kasb
Sanusi says kasb is the locus of legal obligation and a sign for reward and punishment. Why does kasb serve these roles? Because it preserves human involvement without attributing creation to humans.
This is the link to refutation.
4
Examine the refutation of Jabr
Sanusi gives three reasons Jabr is invalid: it denies the necessary (the evident fact of human power), abolishes the locus of obligation, and removes the sign of reward/punishment. Trace each reason in the text.
The phrase 'li-mā fīhi' introduces the reasons.
5
Reflect on why Jabr is bid'a
Sanusi concludes that Jabr is innovation. Reflect on how denying human power undermines the entire structure of Islamic moral theology.
This shows the practical stakes of the doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن تعلُّق هذه القدرة الحادثة بالمقدور مقارنةً لهُ مِنْ غير تأثير .. عبَّرَ أهل السنَّةِ رضي الله عنهم بالكسب ؛ وهو مُتعلَّقُ التكليف الشرعي ، وأمارة على الثواب والعقاب فبطل إذاً مذهب الجبر ؛ وهو إنكار القدرة الحادثة ؛ لما فِيهِ مِنْ جَحْدِ الضرورة ، وإبطالِ محلّ التكليف ، وأمارة الثواب والعقاب ، ومِنْ هنا كانَ بدعة
And regarding the attachment of this created power (al-qudra al-ḥāditha) to the object of power (al-maqdūr) concomitantly with it without effect, the Ahl al-Sunna (may Allah be pleased with them) expressed it as acquisition (al-kasb). It is the locus of legal obligation (al-taklīf al-sharʿī) and a sign (amāra) for reward and punishment. Thus the doctrine of Jabr (compulsion) is invalidated, which is the denial of the created power, because it entails denial of the necessary, abolition of the locus of obligation, and the sign of reward and punishment. Hence it is innovation (bidʿa).
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage defines the technical term 'kasb' (acquisition) and uses it to refute the doctrine of Jabr (fatalism). The author first states that kasb is the relation of the created power to the action without causal influence — it is concomitant but not effective. The Ahl al-Sunna express this as 'kasb'. He then identifies kasb as the locus of legal obligation and a sign for reward and punishment. From this, he concludes that the school of Jabr is false, because Jabr denies the existence of the created power altogether. He gives three reasons why denying created power is invalid: (1) it contradicts what is necessary (i.e., the evident fact that humans have power), (2) it abolishes the locus of obligation (since obligation requires a capacity in the servant), and (3) it removes the sign for reward and punishment. Therefore, Jabr is an innovation (bidʿa).

Key Terms
al-kasb
al-qudra al-ḥāditha
al-taklīf al-sharʿī
amāra
al-jabr
al-bidʿa

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think kasb implies humans have no role at all; it is a form of secret compulsion.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies kasb is the locus of obligation and a sign for reward and punishment, meaning human acquisition is real and morally significant.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why is the doctrine of Jabr invalid?
A) It denies the existence of God.
B) It denies the created power, which is necessary for obligation and a sign for reward/punishment.
C) It affirms human power to create actions.
D) It claims actions are generated from previous actions.

Key Takeaway
Kasb is the Ash'ari term for human acquisition of actions while Allah is the sole creator; it preserves moral responsibility and refutes fatalism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you ever catch yourself thinking, 'It was decreed for me, so I couldn't help it'? How does Sanusi's argument that Jabr is a refuted innovation challenge that excuse in your heart right now?
?
If you truly believed that every action you 'acquire' is the basis for reward and punishment, while Allah alone creates it, would you treat your small daily choices with more reverence or less? What specific change would you make starting tomorrow?
?
When you do a good deed, whose creation do you celebrate? Is it possible that you subtly attribute the deed to your own power, forgetting that your power is created and attaches without effect? How would you humbly acknowledge Allah's sole creative power in your next good action?

Refutation of the Qadariyya Doctrine
Sanusi refutes the Qadariyya claim that humans invent their own actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's two arguments refuting the Qadariyya claim that humans independently create their actions.

Core Idea
The Qadariyya position contradicts tawhid and leads to logical absurdity.

Sanusi now tackles a major theological deviation: the belief that humans invent their own actions independently of divine power. This position, held by the Qadariyya, seems to preserve human responsibility, but it actually compromises the oneness of Allah and leads to rational impossibility. Let's see how he dismantles it.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Qadariyya doctrine
Read the passage definition: the Qadariyya believe the servant invents his actions by the power Allah created in him, according to his own will. This is the claim Sanusi refutes.
Notice the phrase 'يخترع أفعاله' – they attribute actual invention to humans.
2
Follow the first argument – from tawhid
Sanusi says this doctrine is invalid because of the proof of divine oneness. How does claiming human creative power conflict with Allah's uniqueness? Consider what it implies about partners in creation.
If humans truly create, they share in divine attributes.
3
Follow the second argument – logical impossibility
Sanusi then argues that if the human power could truly prevent the eternal power from creating an act, that would make what is possible impossible – a logical contradiction known as tarjīḥ al-marjūḥ. Work through this reasoning step by step.
The action can be related to divine power before human power; preventing that relation is absurd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومذهب القدريَّةِ ؛ وهو كونُ العبدِ يخترعُ أفعاله على وَفْقِ مرادِهِ بالقدرة التي خلق الله تعالى لهُ ؛ لما علمْتَ مِنْ دليل الوحدانية ، واستحالة شريك معَ اللهِ تعالى أيّاً كانَ ويلزمُ فيهِ أيضاً إحالةُ ما عُلِمَ إمكانُهُ ؛ إذ الأفعالُ يصح تعلُّقُ القدرةِ القديمةِ بها قبلَ تعلُّق القدرة الحادثة ، فلو منَعَتها القدرة الحادثةُ للزِمَ مَا ذُكِرَ وترجيحُ المرجوح
And the doctrine of the Qadariyya, which is that the servant invents his actions according to his will by the power that Allah Almighty created for him, [is invalid] because of what you have learned from the proof of divine oneness (dalīl al-waḥdāniyya) and the impossibility of any partner with Allah Almighty. It also necessitates the impossibility of what is known to be possible (iḥālat mā ʿulima imkānuhu), since actions can be related to the eternal power (al-qudra al-qadīma) before the relation of the created power. So if the created power prevented them, then what was mentioned would follow, and the preference of the preponderated (tarjīḥ al-marjūḥ).
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage refutes the Qadariyya, who claim that humans themselves invent their actions using the power created by Allah. Sanusi gives two arguments. First, from the proof of tawḥīd (divine oneness): to ascribe true creative effect to human power implies a partner with Allah in creating actions. Second, a logical argument: an action can be related to the eternal power before the created power relates to it. If the created power then 'prevents' the eternal power (i.e., actually creates the act independently), that would entail that what is possible (the act being created by eternal power) becomes impossible, and this would be a case of 'preferring the preponderated' (tarjīḥ al-marjūḥ) — an absurdity. Thus the Qadariyya position is impossible.

Key Terms
al-qadariyya
al-qudra al-qadīma
al-waḥdāniyya
tarjīḥ al-marjūḥ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Humans have complete free will to create their own actions independently of Allah.
Correction: Sanusi argues that such a belief violates divine oneness (tawhid) and leads to logical absurdity (tarjīḥ al-marjūḥ).

Checkpoint
What is one argument Sanusi uses against the Qadariyya?
A) Humans have no power at all.
B) Both eternal and created powers cannot relate to the same act independently, or it would lead to impossibility.
C) Actions are purely divine creations with no human involvement.
D) The Qadariyya deny the existence of God.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi refutes the Qadariyya by showing their position contradicts tawhid and leads to the logical absurdity of preferring the preponderated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what areas of your life do you instinctively feel that your choices are independent inventions, not dependent on Allah's will? How does this lesson challenge that feeling, and what would change in your daily reliance on Allah if you truly believed all power belongs to Him?
?
When you commit a sin, do you ever downplay its severity by thinking, 'I acted on my own free will'? How should Sanusi's refutation affect your understanding of sin, repentance, and your need for Allah's mercy and guidance?
?
The Qadariyya doctrine leads to logical absurdity. Are you willing to submit your intellect to the truth of tawhid, even when you cannot fully grasp the mystery of divine decree and human responsibility? What practical step can you take today to surrender your limited understanding to Allah's absolute wisdom?

Divine Decree

First Objection and Answer: Reward and Punishment
Sanusi answers objections about God's ability to remove power and about reward/punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's response to the objection that reward and punishment require human agency, and the concept of actions as mere legal signs (amārāt sharʿiyya) indicating divine decree.

Core Idea
Reward and punishment are based on divine signs, not human causation.

Sanusi now faces objections from those who argue that if Allah creates all acts, then reward and punishment lose their basis. He defends divine sovereignty by clarifying that actions are not the cause of reward but merely signs that indicate Allah's pre-eternal decree. Let's examine his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two objections
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the two objections introduced by 'قالوا'. The first concerns Allah's ability to remove created power; the second concerns reward and punishment.
The passage is structured as objection-response pairs.
2
Understand Sanusi's first answer: removal of power
Sanusi first argues that if Allah removes the created power, then He cannot create the act while the power exists—a contradiction. Then he invokes the opponent's principle of al-aṣlaḥ (most beneficial), which forbids removing power after obligation because it harms the servant.
This is a dialectical argument using the opponent's own premise.
3
Grasp the second answer: actions as legal signs
Sanusi asserts that reward and punishment are not caused (muʿallal) by the servant's act. Instead, actions are merely legal signs (amārāt sharʿiyya) that Allah creates in each person to indicate His pre-eternal will for their final outcome.
This removes necessity of human causation for reward.
4
Reflect on the Quranic verse and supplication
Sanusi quotes Hud 11:118 about divine decree and ends with a supplication. This reinforces that all outcomes are by Allah's will and grace.
The verse supports the idea that Allah could have made all people one community but chose otherwise.
5
Answer the checkpoint question
Test your understanding by answering the multiple-choice question based solely on this passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا : لم يزل يقدر عليها ؛ بأنْ يَسلُبَ القدرة الحادثة قلنا : فقد لزمَ إذاً ألا يقدر عليها مع وجودِ القدرةِ الحادثة ! وأيضاً : مِنْ أصلِكُم وجوب مراعاة الأصلح ولا يمكن سلبها عندكم بعد التكليف قالوا : فكيف يثيبه أو يعاقبه على غير فعلِهِ ؟! قلنا : يفعلُ ما شاءَ ، لا يُسأَلُ عما يفعل ، والثواب والعقاب غيرُ مُعلَّلين ، وإنَّما الأفعال أمارات شرعية عليهما ؛ يخلقُ الله تعالى منها في كلِّ مُكلَّف ما يدلُّ شرعاً على ما أرادَ بهِ في عُقباهُ ، فكل ميسر لما خُلِقَ لَهُ ، وَلَوَ شاءَ رَبُّكَ لَجَعَلَ النَّاسَ أُمَّةً وَاحِدَةً ﴾ [هود : ۱۱۸] ، نسأله سبحانه حسْنَ الخاتمة بفضلِهِ
They said: 'He (Allah) has always been able to do it (create the act) by removing the created power.' We said: 'Then it follows that He cannot do it while the created power exists!' Also: 'From your own principle, it is obligatory to observe what is most beneficial (al-aṣlaḥ), and you cannot remove it after obligation.' They said: 'So how does He reward or punish him for an act not his?' We said: 'He does what He wills; He is not questioned about what He does. Reward and punishment are not caused (muʿallalān); rather, actions are only legal signs (amārāt sharʿiyya) for them. Allah creates in each obligated person what legally indicates what He intends for him in his final outcome. So each is facilitated for what he was created for. And if your Lord had willed, He would have made mankind one community [Hud 11:118]. We ask Him, exalted, for a good end by His grace.'
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage contains two objections and Sanusi's responses. First objection: Allah could simply remove the created power to create the act directly. Sanusi replies that then He would be unable to create the act while the created power exists, which is contradictory. He then adds that from the opponent's own principle of al-aṣlaḥ (most beneficial), they cannot claim that Allah removes power after obligation because that would violate the benefit. Second objection: How can Allah reward or punish for an act not truly performed by the servant? Sanusi's answer is twofold. First, Allah is not questioned about His acts; reward and punishment are not caused by the servant's act (they are not muʿallal, i.e., not based on a rational cause). Second, actions are merely legal signs (amārāt) that Allah uses to indicate His intention for the servant's outcome. Allah creates in each person what serves as a sign of what He wills for that person. He then quotes the Quranic verse about divine decree and ends with a supplication.

Key Terms
al-qudra al-ḥāditha
al-aṣlaḥ
al-thawāb
al-ʿiqāb
amārāt sharʿiyya
taysīr

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think reward must be based on human causation; i.e., the servant must produce the act to deserve reward or punishment.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that reward and punishment are not caused (muʿallal) by human acts; rather, acts are mere legal signs (amārāt) that Allah uses to indicate His decree.

Checkpoint
What is Sanusi's response to the objection that Allah cannot remove created power after obligation?
A) He says it is possible because Allah is omnipotent.
B) He says it would violate the principle of al-aṣlaḥ (most beneficial) according to the opponents.
C) He says it is necessary for justice.
D) He says the act is still the servant's creation.

Key Takeaway
Reward and punishment are not caused by human acts but are decreed by Allah; actions are merely signs that indicate His will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your best deeds are not the cause of your salvation, but only signs of what Allah has decreed? How does this free you from pride or despair?
?
When you face a calamity, do you question Allah's justice because you think you didn't 'earn' it? How does this passage command you to surrender your sense of entitlement?
?
If Allah is not questioned about what He does, will you finally stop questioning the parts of your life that don't make sense? What would it cost you to trust His decree without demanding an explanation?

Divine Decree
beginner

Second Objection: Praise and Blame, and the Final Truth
Sanusi answers objection about praise/blame and gives the final position: compelled in the mold of free choice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi defends divine predestination against the objection of praise and blame, and his final formulation that the servant is 'compelled in the mold of free choice.'

Core Idea
Compelled in the mold of free choice: divine decree meets human responsibility.

Sanusi now addresses a second objection: if humans do not truly act, why praise or blame them? He responds concisely, then gives the final truth of the matter. This lesson captures the heart of the Ash'ari position on qadar: the servant is compelled, but in a way that preserves moral accountability.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the objection
Read the objection: if humans do not create their actions, praise and blame seem unjust, and humans would have a valid argument against Allah. Note the Quranic verse they cite.
The objectors assume that reward and punishment require free will.
2
Examine Sanusi's responses
Sanusi gives two brief replies. First, he refers to his earlier answer. Second, he points to the creation of motive and power, and Allah's eternal knowledge, which undermine the objection.
These responses show that divine control does not negate human accountability.
3
Understand the final truth
Sanusi states the final position: the servant is compelled in the mold of free choice. Reflect on how this formulation balances predestination and moral responsibility.
This phrase is a key Ash'ari concept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا : كيفَ يُمدَحُ العبد أو يُذَمُّ على غيرِ ما فعل ؟! ويلزمُ أنْ يكونَ للعبادِ الحجَّةُ في الآخرة ، وقد قال تعالى : لِئَلَّا يَكُونَ لِلنَّاسِ عَلَى اللَّهِ حُجَّةُ بَعْدَ الرُّسُلِ ﴾ [النساء : ١٦٥] . قلنا : مِنْ معنى ما قبلَهُ وأيضاً : يبطل بمسألة خلْقِ الداعي والقدرة ، وبعلمهِ القديم المحيط بكل شيء . والحقُّ : أنَّ العبد مجبورٌ في قالب مختارِ ، فَحَسُنَ فِيهِ رَعْيُ الأمرين على تقدير تسليم أصل التحسين والتقبيح العقليين
They said: 'How is the servant praised or blamed for what he did not do? It would necessitate that servants have an argument (ḥujja) against Allah in the Hereafter, while He, exalted, said: 'So that people would have no argument against Allah after the messengers' [Quran 4:165].' We said: 'From the meaning of what preceded it.' Also: 'It is invalidated by the issue of the creation of the motive (al-dāʿī) and the power, and by His eternal knowledge encompassing everything.' The truth: 'The servant is compelled in the mold of free choice (majbūr fī qālib mukhtār), thus it is good to observe both aspects upon the assumption of acknowledging the principle of rational good and evil (al-taḥsīn wa al-taqbīḥ al-ʿaqliyyayn).'
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This lesson presents the second objection and Sanusi's final summary. The objectors argue that if humans do not truly create their actions, praise and blame are unjust, and humans would have a valid argument against Allah in the Hereafter, contradicting the Quranic verse that denies such argument after messengers. Sanusi gives two brief responses. First, 'from the meaning of what preceded it' — likely referring to his earlier answer about reward/punishment being signs. Second, the objection is invalidated by two issues: (1) the creation of the motive (al-dāʿī) and the power (al-qudra), meaning that Allah creates the motive and power in the servant, so the act is attributed to the servant in a way that still allows praise/blame; (2) Allah's eternal knowledge encompasses everything, so no argument remains. He then states the final truth (al-ḥaqq): the servant is compelled (majbūr) but in a mold of free choice (qālib mukhtār). This formulation allows both divine predestination and human moral responsibility. Sanusi adds that on the assumption of accepting rational good and evil (al-taḥsīn wa al-taqbīḥ al-ʿaqliyyayn), it is fitting to observe both aspects (divine compulsion and human choice).

Key Terms
al-ḥujja
khalq al-dāʿī
al-qudra
al-ʿilm al-qadīm
majbūr fī qālib mukhtār
al-taḥsīn wa al-taqbīḥ al-ʿaqliyyān

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'compelled in the mold of free choice' means pure determinism with no human responsibility.
Correction: Sanusi uses this phrase to affirm that while Allah creates the motive and power, the servant still acts and is accountable, thus praise and blame remain valid.

Checkpoint
What is the 'final truth' (al-ḥaqq) that Sanusi states regarding human action?
A) Humans have absolute free will.
B) Humans are completely compelled with no involvement.
C) The servant is compelled in the mold of free choice.
D) Actions are generated from previous actions.

Key Takeaway
The servant is compelled in the mold of free choice, which allows both divine predestination and human moral responsibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever attributed a sin you committed to 'qadar' to avoid feeling guilty or to excuse yourself from repentance? After this lesson, do you still feel you can use that excuse without contradicting your own sense of responsibility?
?
You believe that every action of yours is created by Allah, yet you feel anger or disappointment at yourself or others for mistakes. How will you hold yourself and others accountable without falling into blaming Allah for what He has decreed?
?
If you knew that your every thought and intention is encompassed by Allah's eternal knowledge, yet you experience them as your own choices, does that make you more conscious of your actions or more passive? What will you do today to exercise your 'mold of free choice' in a way that pleases Allah?

Divine Decree
intermediate
6 min
Answering objections on reward, punishment, and human acts
Sanusi answers objections about divine reward, punishment, and human responsibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi defends the Ash'ari position on reward and punishment by explaining that deeds are merely legal indicators of divine will, not causes, and that human responsibility is preserved through the concept of coercion within a framework of choice.

Core Idea
Reward and punishment are not caused by deeds; deeds are indicators of Allah's decree.

Sanusi now addresses two powerful objections that arise from the Ash'ari doctrine of predestination. If Allah alone creates all actions, how can He reward or punish for them? And how can humans be praised or blamed? The answers hinge on a careful distinction between causation and indication, and culminate in a subtle formulation: the servant is coerced within a mold of choice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the translation. Notice the back-and-forth structure of objection and response.
The passage contains two objections, each followed by an answer.
2
Follow the first objection and answer
Identify the first objection: how can Allah reward or punish for what is not the person's deed? Then study the answer: Allah does as He wills; reward/punishment are not caused by deeds but are legal indicators.
The verse from Hud is cited to reinforce Allah's absolute will.
3
Examine the second objection and answer
The second objection concerns praise and blame. The answer first refers back to the previous point, then adds further refutations based on Allah's creating the impulse and ability, and His eternal knowledge.
4
Grasp the concluding principle
The passage ends with the key formula: the servant is coerced in a mold of choice, which allows both divine predestination and human accountability to coexist.
This is the foundational Ash'ari solution to the problem of free will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا : فكيف يثيبه أو يعاقبه على غير فعلِهِ ؟!
قلنا : يفعلُ ما شاءَ ، لا يُسأَلُ عما يفعل ، والثواب والعقاب غيرُ مُعلَّلين ، وإنَّما الأفعال أمارات شرعية عليهما ؛ يخلقُ الله تعالى منها في كلِّ مُكلَّف ما يدلُّ شرعاً على ما أرادَ بهِ في عُقباهُ ، فكل ميسر لما خُلِقَ لَهُ ، وَلَوَ شاءَ رَبُّكَ لَجَعَلَ النَّاسَ أُمَّةً وَاحِدَةً ﴾ [هود : ۱۱۸] ، نسأله سبحانه حسنَ الخاتمة بفضلِهِ
قالوا : كيفَ يُمدَحُ العبد أو يُذَمُّ على غيرِ ما فعل ؟! ويلزمُ أنْ يكونَ للعبادِ الحجَّةُ في الآخرة ، وقد قال تعالى : لِئَلَّا يَكُونَ لِلنَّاسِ عَلَى اللَّهِ حُجَّةُ بَعْدَ الرُّسُلِ ﴾ [النساء : ١٦٥] .
قلنا : مِنْ معنى ما قبلَهُ
وأيضاً : يبطل بمسألة خلْقِ الداعي والقدرة ، وبعلمهِ القديم المحيط بكل شيء .
والحقُّ : أنَّ العبد مجبورٌ في قالب مختارِ ، فَحَسُنَ فِيهِ رَعْيُ الأمرين على تقدير تسليم أصل التحسين والتقبيح العقليين
They said: How does He reward or punish him for other than his deed? We said: He does what He wills; He is not asked about what He does. Reward and punishment are not caused [by the deed]; rather, deeds are only legal indicators of them. Allah creates from them in every morally responsible person that which legally indicates what He intended for him in his final outcome. So everyone is eased toward what he was created for. Had your Lord willed, He would have made mankind one community [Hud 11:118]. We ask Him for a good end by His grace. They said: How is a servant praised or blamed for other than what he did? And it would necessitate that the servants have proof on the Day of Resurrection, while He said: So that mankind would have no argument against Allah after the messengers [Nisa 4:165]. We said: That is from the meaning of what preceded it. Also: it is refuted by the creation of the impulse and the ability, and by His eternal knowledge encompassing everything. And the truth is: the servant is coerced in a mold of choice, so both matters are considered in him upon the assumption of accepting the principle of rational good and evil.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage consists of two objections and answers concerning the Ash'ari position on divine reward, punishment, and human responsibility. The first objection asks how Allah can reward or punish a person for something that person did not do. The answer asserts that Allah is not questioned about His actions; reward and punishment are not caused by human deeds but are merely legal indicators that Allah creates in the person to show His decree. The verse from Hud is cited to emphasize that Allah's will is ultimate. The second objection asks how a person can be praised or blamed for actions not their own, which would give humans an argument against Allah. The answer first refers back to the previous reply, then adds that the objection is refuted by considering Allah's creation of the impulse and ability within the person, and by His eternal encompassing knowledge. Finally, a key doctrinal summary is given: the truth is that the servant is coerced within a mold of choice ('abd majbūr fī qālib mukhtār'), meaning that human responsibility is preserved by accepting the framework of rational good and evil (taḥsīn wa taqbīḥ 'aqliyyān). The explanation follows the sequential order of the objections and answers.

Key Terms
ثواب
عقاب
أمارات شرعية
جبر
قالب اختيار
تحسين وتقبيح عقليين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Ash'aris deny human responsibility entirely, leaving no room for praise or blame.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the servant is 'coerced in a mold of choice,' meaning responsibility is maintained through the framework of rational good and evil, which allows for praise and blame even if acts are ultimately from Allah.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between Allah's decree and human acts?
A) Allah rewards based on human acts.
B) Human acts are legal indicators of Allah's reward and punishment.
C) Allah is not involved in human acts.
D) Humans create their own acts independently.

Key Takeaway
Deeds are not causes of reward or punishment but legal indicators of Allah's decree, and human responsibility is preserved through the concept of 'coerced in a mold of choice' along with rational good and evil.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that your deeds are not the cause of your reward or punishment, but merely indicators of Allah's decree, does that free you from relying on your own actions? Or does it trouble you because you feel your efforts are meaningless? In light of this lesson, how will you trust Allah's justice without depending on your own works?
?
Sanusi says the servant is 'coerced in a mold of choice.' Have you ever felt the tension between your sense of choice and the reality of Allah's absolute control? When you sin, do you blame yourself or resign to predestination? This lesson calls you to accept both: truly repent while acknowledging that all is from Allah. How will you embody that balance in your next moment of weakness?
?
The passage ends with 'We ask Him for a good end by His grace.' Do you genuinely believe that your final outcome is entirely up to Allah's grace, not your deeds? Is your hope in His grace or in your own righteousness? Let this question lead you to a specific dua today, asking for a good end purely by His favor.

God's Creation of Actions and No Obligation
Sanusi states the Sunni position on God's creation of actions and rejection of divine obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni (Ash'ari) position that God is not obligated to create what is best for His creatures, and that all actions equally indicate His power.

Core Idea
God is not obligated; all actions equally point to His sovereignty.

Sanusi here lays down a cornerstone of Sunni theology: God's actions are not constrained by any obligation to create what is best. He creates servants, their actions, and reward/punishment purely by His will. This passage refutes the Mu'tazili doctrine of al-aṣlaḥ and establishes that good and evil actions are equal in pointing to God's absolute power.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and its English translation. Notice the chapter heading and the list of things that are possible for God.
2
Identify what is possible for God
Find the three things Sanusi says are among the possible things (al-jā'izāt) for God: creating servants, creating their actions, and creating reward and punishment for those actions.
He emphasizes that none of this is obligatory upon God.
3
Understand the logical consequence
Observe the conditional argument: if God were obliged to consider what is good or better (al-salāḥ or al-aṣlaḥ), then there would be no basis for religious obligation (taklīf) or for worldly and afterlife trials (miḥna). Since these exist, God is not so obliged.
This is a refutation of the Mu'tazili view.
4
Reflect on the equality of actions
Read the final statement that all actions, good or evil, beneficial or harmful, are equal in indication (dalāla). Think about what that means: they all equally point to God as Creator and to His absolute power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل [ في خلق العباد وأفعالهم وما يتعلق بذلك ] ومِنَ الجائزاتِ في حقِّهِ تعالى : خَلْقُ العبادِ ، وخلقُ أعمالهم ، وخلْقُ الثوابِ والعقاب عليها ، لا يجب عليهِ شيءٌ مِنْ ذلكَ ، ولا مراعاة صلاح ولا أصلح ، وإلا وجبَ ألا يكون تكليف ولا محنة دنيوية ولا أخروية ، والأفعالُ كلُّها ؛ خيرُها وشرها ، نفعُها وضرُّها . . مستوية في الدلالة
Chapter [on the creation of servants and their actions and what pertains to that]. And among the possible things with respect to Him—exalted is He—are: creating servants, creating their actions, and creating reward and punishment for them. Nothing of that is obligatory upon Him, nor [is there] any consideration of what is good or better. Otherwise, it would be necessary that there be no obligation [taklīf] nor any worldly or afterlife trial. And all actions—their good and evil, their benefit and harm—are equal in indication.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a concise statement of the Sunni (Ash'ari) position on divine action and human agency. It begins with a chapter heading indicating the topic: the creation of servants, their actions, and related matters. Sanusi then declares that it is within God's possibility (jā'iz) to create servants, their actions, and the reward and punishment for those actions. He emphasizes that God is not obligated to do any of this—He is not required to create, nor to consider what is 'good' or 'better' (al-salāḥ wa al-aṣlaḥ). The reason given is that if He were obliged to create only what is good or best, then there would be no valid basis for religious obligation (taklīf) or for worldly and afterlife trials (miḥna). In other words, the very existence of tests and hardships—and the fact that some people are punished—shows that God's actions are not constrained by considerations of what is optimal from a human perspective. Finally, Sanusi asserts that all actions, whether good or evil, beneficial or harmful, are equal in their indication (dalāla)—that is, they all equally point to God as their Creator and to His absolute power. This is a direct refutation of the Mu'tazili doctrine that God must create what is best for His servants (al-aṣlaḥ).

Key Terms
خلق (khalq)
جائز (jā'iz)
واجب (wājib)
صلاح (ṣalāḥ)
أصلح (aṣlaḥ)
تكليف (taklīf)
محنة (miḥna)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God is morally obligated to create what is best for His creatures.
Correction: Sunni theology holds that nothing is obligatory upon God; all actions are equally within His power and will.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why would God's obligation to create what is best (al-aṣlaḥ) lead to the negation of religious obligation (taklīf)?
A) Because God would then be forced to punish everyone equally
B) Because there would be no basis for trials and hardships in this world and the afterlife
C) Because humans would have no free will
D) Because good and evil would become indistinguishable

Key Takeaway
God is not obligated to create what is best; all actions, good and evil, equally indicate His absolute power and sovereignty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that God is not obligated to create what is best for you. When you face a trial or hardship, do you secretly resent God for not giving you what you think you deserve? How can you train yourself to accept His decree without demanding an explanation?
?
Since all actions—your good deeds and your sins—are equally created by God and point to His power, does that make you feel your choices are meaningless? Or does it deepen your humility before the One who made you responsible? Take a moment to examine your heart: do you sometimes obey Him hoping He will owe you something in return?
?
If God owes you nothing, and every breath is a pure gift, how does that change the way you pray, worship, and repent today? Are you ready to serve Him without expecting any reward—simply because He is the only true Sovereign?

Divine Creation of Actions and Justice
Sanusi affirms divine creation of actions and negates obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God creates all actions and their outcomes by pure grace and justice, without any obligation or motive.

Core Idea
God's creation and justice are pure grace, not obligation.

Sanusi here articulates a core Ash'ari doctrine: God's actions are not constrained by any external obligation. He creates servants, their deeds, and reward or punishment entirely by His will. This passage defends divine freedom and refutes the idea that God must act for a purpose or reward based on merit.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Let the rhythm of Sanusi's concise style sink in.
2
Identify what is possible for God
Notice the list: creation of servants, their actions, and reward/punishment. All are possible (jāʼizāt) for God, not obligatory.
3
Understand the argument against obligation
Sanusi argues that if God were obliged to consider the good or best, there would be no real trial (taklīf). Reflect on this implication.
4
Grasp the equality of all actions
All actions, good and evil, equally point to God's power, knowledge, and will. No action adds perfection or deficiency to God.
5
Contemplate grace and justice
God honors some and punishes others without any external cause—pure grace and justice. Both demonstrate His dominion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل * في خلق العباد وأفعالهم وما يتعلق بذلك * ومِنَ الجائزاتِ في حقِّهِ تعالى : خَلْقُ العبادِ ، وخلقُ أعمالهم ، وخلْقُ الثوابِ والعقاب عليها ، لا يجب عليهِ شيءٌ مِنْ ذلكَ ، ولا مراعاة صلاح ولا أصلح ، وإلا وجبَ ألا يكون تكليف ولا محنة دنيوية ولا أخروية ، والأفعالُ كلُّها ؛ خيرُها وشرها ، نفعُها وضرُّها . . مستوية في الدلالة على باهر قدرتِهِ جلَّ وعزَّ وسعة علمه ونفوذ إرادتِهِ . لا يتطرَّقُ لذاتِهِ العليَّةِ مِنْ ذلك كمال ولا نقص . كانَ اللهُ ولا شيء معَهُ ، وهو الآن على ما كانَ عليه ، فأكرمَ سبحانَهُ مَنْ شاءَ بما لا يُكيَّفُ مِنْ أنواع النعيمِ بمجرَّدِ فضله ، لا لميل إليه ، أو قضاء حقٌّ وجبَ لَهُ عليهِ ، وعدل فيمَنْ شاءَ بما لا يُطاقُ وصفُهُ مِنْ أصنافِ الجحيم ، لا لإشفاء غيظ ولا لضررٍ نالَهُ مِنْ قِبَلِهِ • وكلا النوعينِ دال على سَعَةِ مُلْكِهِ ، وانقياد جميعِ الممكنات لإرادتِهِ ، وعدم تعاصيها على باهر قدرته ، كل منها واقع على ما ينبغي مِنْ جريه على وَفْقِ علمه وإرادتِهِ ، مِنْ غيرِ أنْ يتجدَّدَ له بذلكَ كمال أو نقص حالاً ولا مالاً
Section on the creation of servants and their actions and what pertains to that. Among the possible things with respect to God, exalted, are: the creation of servants, the creation of their actions, and the creation of reward and punishment upon them. Nothing of that is obligatory upon Him, nor is consideration of what is good or what is best (islah or aslah). Otherwise, it would necessitate that there be no obligation (taklif) nor worldly nor otherworldly trial. All actions, good and evil, beneficial and harmful, are equal in indicating His overwhelming power, vast knowledge, and effective will. No perfection or deficiency attaches to His exalted essence from that. God existed with nothing else, and He is now as He was. So He honored whom He will with types of bliss that cannot be described, by His mere grace, not due to inclination toward them, nor due to fulfilling a right that was due to them from Him. And He was just to whom He will with types of hell that cannot be described, not to satisfy anger nor because of harm that reached Him from them. Both types indicate the vastness of His dominion, the submission of all possible things to His will, and the lack of disobedience to His overwhelming power. Each occurs as it should, flowing in accordance with His knowledge and will, without any perfection or deficiency, state or property, being renewed for Him by that.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement on divine actions. It begins by listing what is possible for God: creating servants, their actions, and reward/punishment. No obligation on God, nor consideration of islah (the good) or aslah (the best). It then argues that if obligation existed, there would be no real trial. All actions equally indicate divine power, knowledge, and will. God's essence is unaffected. Then it describes God's eternal existence and His bestowing grace and justice without any motive or obligation. The passage concludes that both types (grace and justice) demonstrate His dominion, the submission of all possible things, and that no perfection is added to God.

Correction: The passage states clearly that nothing in creation is obligatory upon God, and He acts by pure grace and justice without any external motive.

A) That God is obligated to reward good and punish evil
B) That God's power and will are limited by human actions
C) That God's dominion is vast and all things submit to His will
D) That God gains perfection from creating

Key Takeaway
God creates all actions and their consequences without obligation, and His grace and justice equally manifest His absolute sovereignty.

?

?

Human Acquisition and Divine Creation of Actions
Sanusi defines the acquired act and explains divine creation of human actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari doctrine of kasb (acquisition) and how human actions are created by God while being acquired by the servant.

Core Idea
Humans acquire actions; God alone creates them.

This passage from Sanusi's Umm al-Barahin lays out the Ash'ari position on human actions, a central topic in kalam. It defines when a person is called an 'acquirer' (muktasib) versus 'compelled' (mujbar), and emphasizes that all actions—and even the selves that 'contain' them—are created by God. Let's unpack the key distinctions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic text once, then the English translation. Notice the key terms: قدرة, مقدور, مختار, مكتسب, مضطر, مجبر.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the two categories of human action
The passage defines when a servant is called 'free/acquirer/agent' and when 'compelled/coerced'. What condition determines which term applies?
Look for the phrase 'قدرةً تقارنُهُ'.
3
Examine divine creation of knowledge and will
The passage explains that God may or may not create knowledge and will in the servant along with the power and the act. Why does this matter for the debate on free will?
This refines the Ash'ari position.
4
Understand the container analogy
Read the line about 'الذوات كالظروف' and its explanation. What does this analogy teach about God's sole creative power?
Both container and contained are created by God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قدرةً تقارنُهُ يُسمى العبد في الاصطلاح مختاراً ومكتسباً وفاعلاً ، وإلا سُمِّيَ مُضطراً ومجبوراً ، ثم قد يخلق الله سبحانَهُ معَ هذين الفعلينِ - وهما القدرة والمقدور - علماً للعبدِ وإرادةً لِمَا خلقَ فيهِ ، وتارةً لا يخلق له ذلكَ ، كما أنَّهُ تعالى معَ إفرادِهِ الفعل بالخلْقِ دون القدرة قد يخلقُ للعبدِ شعوراً بذلك ، وقد لا . [ الذواتُ ظروف للأفعال المخلوقة فيها ] وبالجملة : فالذواتُ كالظروفِ للأفعال المخلوقة فيها ، يخلق الله تعالى منها ما شاء وكيفَ شاءَ ، والظرفُ والمظروفُ فعلُ اللهِ تعالى ، لا تأثير لبعض في بعض ، فتباركَ مَنْ لا شريكَ لهُ في مُلْكِهِ ، ولا مُدبَّرَ معَهُ سواه ، ولا يُسأَل عما يفعل جلَّ وعلا
A power that accompanies it is called, in technical terminology, a free, acquired, and acting servant; otherwise he is called compelled and coerced. Then God, exalted may He be, may create with these two acts—namely the power and the thing empowered—knowledge for the servant and will for what He created in him, and sometimes He does not create that for him. Just as He, exalted, when He singularizes the act in creation without the power, may create for the servant awareness of that, and may not. [Selves are containers for the acts created in them.] In summary: selves are like containers for the acts created in them; God, exalted, creates from them whatever He wills and however He wills. The container and the contained are both the act of God, exalted; no one has any influence over another. So blessed is He who has no partner in His dominion, and no disposer with Him other than Him, and He is not asked about what He does, mighty and majestic.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage defines the Ash'ari doctrine of human acquisition (kasb) and divine creation of human actions. It begins by stating that when a human possesses a power (qudra) that accompanies the act, that human is technically called 'free' (mukhtār), 'acquirer' (muktasib), and 'agent' (fāʿil); otherwise, if no accompanying power, the person is called 'compelled' (muḍṭarr) and 'coerced' (majbūr). Then it explains that God may create knowledge and will in the servant along with the two things—the power and the thing empowered (the action)—or may not create them. Similarly, when God creates the act alone without the power, He may or may not create awareness in the servant. The passage then emphasizes an analogy: the selves (dhawāt) are like containers (ẓurūf) for the acts created in them. Both the container (the self) and the contained (the act) are created by God, and no part has any effect upon another. It concludes with a doxology affirming God's sole sovereignty and that He is not questioned about what He does.

Key Terms
قدرة (qudra)
مقدور (maqdūr)
مختار (mukhtār)
مكتسب (muktasib)
فاعل (fāʿil)
مضطر (muḍṭarr)
مجبر (majbūr)
ذوات (dhawāt)
ظرف (ẓarf)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazilite belief that humans independently create their own actions.
Correction: The Ash'ari position is that all actions are created by God; humans merely acquire them through an accompanying power that God creates.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when is a servant called 'acquirer' (muktasib)?
A) When he acts independently of God's power.
B) When a power (qudra) accompanies his act.
C) When he has no power and is compelled.
D) When he creates the act himself.

Key Takeaway
Human actions are created by God and acquired by the servant through an accompanying power; neither the self nor the act has any independent effect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly believe that God created that act? How does that affect your repentance and reliance on Him alone?
?
If every action you do is created by God, what does that mean for your pride in your good deeds? Are you still the one deserving praise?
?
The passage says God is not asked about what He does. Is there any event in your life you are struggling to accept because you question God's wisdom? How does this lesson challenge that attitude?

Divine Justice on Judgment Day: Every Right Restored
Hadiths about God as the Judge settling accounts on Judgment Day.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that on Judgment Day, Allah will settle all accounts with perfect justice, including even the smallest rights, and that deeds will be the measure.

Core Idea
On Judgment Day, every wrong will be righted, even a slap, through good and bad deeds.

This lesson presents a collection of hadiths that illustrate the comprehensive nature of Allah's justice on the Day of Judgment. The Prophet (peace be upon him) teaches that no one will enter Paradise until all accounts are settled, down to the smallest injustice. These narrations prepare us to understand the absolute fairness of the divine judgment.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadiths carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the repeated emphasis on even a slap being accounted for.
The passage contains multiple narrations; focus on the shared message.
2
Consider the Companions' question
The Companions ask how retribution can occur when people come naked and without physical forms. This highlights a deeper point: material rights must still be satisfied.
The answer that deeds are used shows the spiritual nature of justice.
3
Understand the role of deeds
The Prophet explains that good and bad deeds will serve as the currency for settling accounts. Reflect on how this makes every action significant.
4
Connect to broader Islamic teachings
These hadiths reinforce the belief that Allah is perfectly just and that no injustice, however small, will be overlooked. Consider how this affects your view of accountability.
This lesson is part of the wider topic of qadar and divine justice.

الملكُ ، أنا الديَّانُ ، ولا ينبغي لأحدٍ من أهل الجنة أن يدخل الجنة ولأحد من أهل النار عنده حق حتى أُقِصَّهُ منه حتى اللطمةُ » ، قال : قلنا : كيف وإنَّا إنما نأتي الله عز وجل عراة غرلاً بهماً ؟ قال : « بالحسنات والسيئاتِ » ، وفي رواية الطبراني في مسند الشاميين » ( ١٥٦ ) : « فيقولُ : أنا الديَّانُ ، لا تظالم اليوم ، وعزتي لا يجاوزُني اليومَ ظلم ظالم ولو لطمةَ كفّ بكفّ أو يد على ، وروى ابن أبي شيبة في ( المصنف » ( ٣٦٧٩٤ ) قال : ( بلغني أن الله تبارك وتعالى يقول يوم القيامة : يا بني آدم ؛ إنا قد أنصتنا لكم منذ خلقناكم إلى يومكم هذا ، فأنصتوا لنا نقرأ أعمالكم عليكم ) (۱) ومثل ذلك ما ورد من الخطابات بين الله تعالى وعباده .
The King, I am the Judge. It is not fitting for anyone from the people of Paradise to enter Paradise while someone from the people of Hell has a right against him until I exact retribution for it, even for a slap.' He (the Companion) said: We said, 'How can that be when we come to Allah, mighty and majestic, naked, uncircumcised, and dumb?' He said: 'By good deeds and evil deeds.' And in a narration of al-Ṭabarānī in Musnad al-Shāmiyyīn (156): 'He says: I am the Judge; no oppression today; by My Might, no oppression of an oppressor will pass by Me today, even a slap of a hand by a hand or a hand on [something].' And Ibn Abī Shayba narrated in al-Muṣannaf (36794) said: 'It has reached me that Allah, blessed and exalted, says on the Day of Resurrection: O children of Adam, indeed We have listened to you since We created you until this day of yours, so listen to Us as We recite your deeds to you.' And similar to that are what have been transmitted of discourses between Allah the Exalted and His servants.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage is a collection of hadith quotations illustrating God's justice on the Day of Judgment. The first hadith states that God will settle all accounts, even for a slap, before anyone enters Paradise. The Companions ask how this is possible when people come naked, uncircumcised, and dumb; the answer is that good and bad deeds will be weight. Al-Ṭabarānī's version emphasizes that no oppression will go unaddressed. Ibn Abī Shayba reports a hadith where God says He has listened to people since creation and now they should listen as He recites their deeds. These narrations show that God communicates with His servants on that day.

Misconception: Only major sins are accounted for on Judgment Day.
Correction: These hadiths show that even a slap will be accounted for, demonstrating that Allah's justice covers all actions, no matter how small.

Allah's justice on Judgment Day is so precise that every single right, even a slap, will be settled using deeds as the currency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Are you prepared to have that exact deed weighed against your good deeds on the Day when even a slap is accounted for? What will you do today to seek forgiveness or make amends before that Day?
?
If you were to stand before Allah right now with your deeds recited to you, would any of them be ones you regret but have never tried to rectify? This hadith says every right will be settled. How does that make you feel about your unresolved conflicts?
?
The Prophet's companions were struck by how justice could be done without bodies. But the answer came: deeds. How often do you think about your deeds as the currency of your afterlife? Does this motivate you to increase good deeds not just for reward but to settle debts?

Applying Tamānuʿ to Refute Human Causal Power
Sanusi begins applying the tamānuʿ proof to deny human creative power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the tamānuʿ (mutual hindrance) proof, used to establish God's oneness, also refutes the claim that humans independently create their own actions.

Core Idea
If humans create their own actions, they rival God's will—the tamānuʿ proof applies.

Sanusi now extends the tamānuʿ proof, previously used to argue for God's oneness, to the doctrine of human actions. The Qadariyya claimed that humans produce their own deeds through a created power independent of God. Sanusi argues that this claim leads to the same logical absurdity as polytheism: if a human's will could override God's will, then God would be impotent. This passage introduces that application.

Guided Path
1
Understand the tamānuʿ proof's original purpose
Recall that tamānuʿ shows that multiple gods would conflict and lead to impotence. Sanusi now applies the same logic to human actions.
2
Identify the Qadariyya claim
The Qadariyya assert that human created power (qudra ḥāditha) effectively causes actions, independent of God's power and will. Find this in the passage.
The passage states: 'القدرية القائلين بأن القدرة الحادثة للعباد هي المؤثرة'.
3
See the necessary consequence
Sanusi argues that if a human's created power could act against God's will, it would be like a second deity whose will conflicts, necessitating impotence in God—an impossibility.
The passage cuts off, but the argument is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصلُ في تفرده بتخانه با يجاد جميع الافعال، وأن [افضل السواه] بهذا الدليل بعيينه - أعني : دليل التمانع - نستدل على أنَّهُ جلَّ وعلا هو الموجدُ لأفعال العبادِ ، ولا تأثير لقُدَرِهم الحادثة فيها ، بل هي موجودة مقارنة لها يعني : أنَّ الدليل على ردّ مذهب القدرية القائلين بأنَّ القدرة الحادثة للعبادِ هي المؤثرةُ في أفعالهم على وَفْقِ اختيارهم ، ولا تأثير للقدرةِ القديمة أصلاً في تلك الأفعالِ الاختياريَّةِ ، ولا جريان لها على وَفْقِ إرادتِهِ ، جلَّ وتعالى عما يقولُ الظالمون علوّاً كبيراً. هو دليلُ التمانع السابق . ووجههُ : أَنَّ اللازم فيهِ في تعدُّدِ الآلهة ثبوتُ العجز للإلهِ عندَ عدم نفوذ إرادته ، وذلكَ بعينه لازم في مذهب القدريَّةِ؛ فإنَّهم جعلوا تعلُّقَ
A chapter on His exclusivity in [creating] all actions, and that [the actions of others?] by this same proof - I mean: the proof of mutual hindrance (tamānuʿ) - we infer that He, exalted and majestic, is the creator of the actions of servants, and there is no effect for their created powers in them, rather they are existent concurrent with them. Meaning: the proof for rejecting the doctrine of the Qadariyya who say that the created power of the servants is the effective agent in their actions according to their choice, and there is no effect for the eternal power at all in those voluntary actions, and they do not proceed according to His will - exalted and far above what the wrongdoers say, greatly - is the previous proof of mutual hindrance. And its face: that the necessary consequence in it concerning the multiplicity of gods is the establishment of impotence for the god when His will does not prevail, and that same consequence is necessary in the doctrine of the Qadariyya; for they make the attachment...
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of a new section where Sanusi applies the tamānuʿ (mutual hindrance) proof, previously used to establish God's oneness, to the issue of human actions. He argues that just as multiple gods would imply each god's impotence due to conflicting wills, so too the Qadariyya (those who believe humans create their own actions) effectively posit a similar conflict: if a human's created power can produce actions independently of God's will and power, then God's will would be thwarted, implying impotence. Therefore, the tamānuʿ proof refutes both polytheism and the Qadariyya doctrine. The passage also clarifies that the created power (qudra ḥāditha) is not effective; rather, actions exist concurrently with human power (i.e., God creates both the action and the power simultaneously). The proof rests on the premise that if a created agent could act against God's will, it would be like a second god whose will conflicts with God's. Hence, the tamānuʿ proof applies. The passage is cut off, indicating continuation.

Correction: Sanusi shows it also refutes the Qadariyya claim that humans independently create their actions, as that would imply a conflict with God's will.

?
If you truly believed that your created power has no effect whatsoever on your actions, would you still feel responsible for your sins? How does this lesson reshape your understanding of accountability and your need for God's mercy?

The Qadariyya Claim and Its Implication of Shirk
Sanusi states the Qadariyya claim and exposes its implication of shirk.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qadariyya claim that human power prevents divine power leads to affirming a partner for Allah and attributing incapacity to Him.

Core Idea
Claiming human power over God’s is shirk.

Sanusi begins by laying out the Qadariyya position: that the slave's power and will can actually prevent Allah's power and will from attaching to an action. He then highlights the devastating theological consequence of this view, showing that it necessarily implies a partner for Allah and brands Him with the defect of incapacity.

Guided Path
1
Read the Qadariyya claim
Read the first sentence carefully, noting that they claim the slave's power and will prevent Allah's.
2
Identify the logical contradiction
Notice that Sanusi points out the Qadariyya admit that Allah's power and will attach to all possibles, yet they claim His power is prevented by the slave's.
This is the core problem.
3
Understand the implication
Sanusi then asserts that this statement amounts to affirming a partner for Allah and branding Him with incapacity. Consider why this is a necessary consequence.
If the weaker power overcomes the stronger, that implies the stronger is weak.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قدرة العبد وإرادتِهِ بالفعل مانعةٌ مِنْ تعلُّقِ قدرةِ اللهِ تعالى وإرادتِهِ بذلكَ الفعلِ، معَ القطع بأنَّ ذلكَ الفعلَ مِنْ جملة الممكناتِ التي قام البرهانُ القطعي على وجوبِ تعلقِ قدرة الله تعالى وإرادته بوصف العموم بجميعها. فصار إذاً هذا الفعل قد توجَّهَتْ نحوه قدرة العبد وقدرة مولانا جل وعلا، وإرادة العبدِ وإرادة مولانا سبحانه وتعالى؛ لما عرفْتَ مِنْ عموم تعلّق قدرته تعالى وإرادتِهِ، ثم زعمَتِ القدريَّةُ مجوس هذهِ الأمة: أنَّ الذي نفذ وأثَرَ في الفعل - والحالة هذهِ ـ إنَّما هو أضعفُ القدرتين وأضعفُ الإرادتين؛ وهما قدرة العبد الفقير الحقير وإرادته! وهل هذا القولُ الشنيع إلا قول بإثباتِ الشريك له تعالى، ووَسْمٌ لَهُ بنقيصة العجز وغلبة الغيرِ له؟! وإذا كانَ عجْزُ الإله بتقدير نفوذ إرادة إله آخر يماثلُهُ قادحاً هيَّتِهِ، وموجباً لنقصِهِ وعدم ذاتِهِ[فإنه يمتنع].. فكيف بعجزه لنفوذ قدرةِ عبده وإرادته؟! ولا ينفعُهم ما يجيبونَ بهِ مِنْ عدم لزومِ عجزِهِ تعالى عن الفعل الذي أوجدَهُ عبدُهُ؛ قالوا: لأنَّهُ تعالى قادرٌ أَنْ يُوجِدَ ذلكَ الفعل؛ بأنْ يسلب عبده القدرة عليه والإرادة له، ويلجئه إلى الفعل كما يفعلُ بالمرتعش ونحوه؛ لأنَّا نقولُ: عجز الإله وكونه مغلوباً على إيجادِ ممكن ما.. يستحيلُ مطلقاً، وهذا الجواب منهم اقتضى أنَّهُ تعالى لا يتمكَّنُ مِنْ إيجادِ فعل العبدِ إلا عند عدم قدرة العبد وإرادتِهِ، أَمَّا معَ وجودِهما فإنَّ ذلك الفعل الممكن يتعاصى عليه، ولا يتمكَّنُ مِنْ إيجادِهِ، وتغلبه عليه قدرة العبد وإرادته! فما أشبة ضلالهم هذا بمَنْ يصفُ إنساناً بقوَّةٍ عظيمةٍ لا يغلبُهُ معَها أحدٌ، ولذلك الإنسانِ عبيد، ويقولُ: إِنَّ ذلكَ السَّيِّدَ القوي في غاية لا يغلب واحداً مِنْ أولئكَ العبيد إلا إذا احتالَ عليهِ؛ بأنْ يسلبَهُ أسبابَ القوَّةِ مِنَ الأكل ونحوه حتى لا تكونَ للعبدِ قدرة أصلاً، أَمَّا إذا مكَّنَهُ مِنَ الاتصاف بقدرةٍ، وإنْ كانَتْ أضعف بكثيرِ مِنْ قدرته.. لم يقدر أن يفعل معه فعلاً تتوجه إليه قدرة ذلك العبد وإرادته، وصارَتْ قدرة ذلك العبدِ وإرادتُهُ تغلبانِ قدرةَ سيّدِهِ الموصوفِ بغايةِ القوَّةِ! هذا نظيرُ ما تخيَّلوهُ مِنَ الجواب، فنعوذُ باللهِ مِنَ الخِذلانِ، وأن تلعب بعقولنا التوهمات والشيطانُ. على أنَّ جوابهم المذكور لا يستقيم على أصلهم الفاسدِ مِنْ وجوبِ مراعاة الصلاح والأصلح عليهِ تعالى، وأنه يستحيل في حقه تعالى أن يسلب العبد القدرة التي خلق لهُ بعدَ أنْ كلَّفَهُ، بل يجبُ أنْ يمدَّهُ بما تتيسر بهِ عليهِ الأَفعال.
The power and will of the slave with respect to an action prevent the attachment of the power and will of Allah Most High to that action, while being certain that that action is among the possible things for which the definitive proof has established the necessity of the attachment of the power of Allah Most High and His will in a general manner to all of them. So this action therefore has been directed towards it the power of the slave and the power of our Master Glorified and Exalted, and the will of the slave and the will of our Master Glorified and Exalted; because you have known the generality of the attachment of His power and His will. Then the Qadariyya – the Magians of this ummah – claimed: that which executed and had effect in the action – in this state – is only the weaker of the two powers and the weaker of the two wills; and they are the power of the humble, contemptible slave and his will! Is this odious statement anything but a statement affirming a partner to Him Most High, and branding Him with the defect of incapacity and the overcoming of others over Him?! And if the incapacity of a deity by supposing the penetration of the will of another deity similar to him is detrimental to his dignity and necessitating his deficiency and the nonexistence of his essence [then it is impossible]... then how [can it be] with His incapacity due to the penetration of the power of His slave and his will?! And their response does not benefit them, that there is no necessary implication of His incapacity Most High regarding the action which His slave has brought into existence; they said: because He Most High is able to bring that action into existence by stripping His slave of the power and will for it, and compelling him to the action as He does with a tremulous person and the like; for we say: the incapacity of the deity and His being overcome in bringing into existence any possible thing is absolutely impossible, and this response from them implies that He Most High cannot bring into existence the action of the slave except when the slave lacks power and will, but with their existence, that possible action becomes stubborn to Him, and He cannot bring it into existence, and the power and will of the slave overcome Him! How similar is this misguidance of theirs to one who describes a human being with great strength that no one can overcome, and that human being has slaves, and says: that strong master in extremity cannot overcome any one of those slaves unless he uses a trick against him by stripping him of the means of strength such as food and the like so that the slave has no power at all, but if he enables him to be described with power, even if it is much weaker than his power... he cannot do with him an action towards which the power and will of that slave are directed, and the power and will of that slave overcome the power of his master described with utmost strength! This is the analogue of what they imagined from the response, so we seek refuge with Allah from abandonment, and that delusions and Satan play with our minds. Moreover, that response of theirs is not consistent with their corrupt principle of the necessity of observing what is beneficial and most beneficial for Him Most High, and that it is impossible in His right Most High to strip the slave of the power which He created for him after He had obligated him, rather He must supply him with what makes actions easy for him.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Qadariyya (an early theological sect) who claimed that human power and will can prevent God's power and will from acting on an action. Sanusi begins by stating the Qadariyya position: the slave's power and will actually prevent God's power and will from attaching to that action, even though that action is among all possible things, and God's power and will must attach to all possibles. He then points out a contradiction: if this were so, both the slave's and God's power and will are directed towards the action, yet the Qadariyya claim that the weaker of the two (the slave's) is the one that actually takes effect. Sanusi calls this an odious statement that implies a partner for God and brands Him with incapacity and being overcome. He makes an analogical argument: if the incapacity of a deity due to another equal deity would be detrimental to his dignity and necessitate his nonexistence as a deity, then how can it be that God is incapable due to the power of His slave? Then he addresses a possible response: the Qadariyya might say that God is able to bring about the action by stripping the slave of power and will and compelling him, as He does with an involuntary tremor. Sanusi refutes this by saying that this response still implies that God cannot bring about the action when the slave has power and will; that is, God's power is hindered by the slave's power, which is absurd. He then gives a vivid analogy: a master of great strength who cannot overcome his slave unless he first strips the slave of his strength through starvation etc., but if the slave has any strength, the master cannot act. This is exactly what the Qadariyya claim about God. Finally, Sanusi adds that even this response is inconsistent with the Qadariyya's own principle that God must observe what is beneficial and most beneficial for His creatures, because it would require God to remove the very power He gave the slave after commanding him, which they hold to be impossible. The passage concludes with a plea for refuge from misguidance.

Key Terms
القدرية
قدرة العبد
قدرة الله
إرادة العبد
إرادة الله
الشرك
العجز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that human free will requires that God's will does not apply to human actions.
Correction: Sanusi shows that this leads to shirk and impossibility because all possibles are subject to God's will and power.

Checkpoint
What does Sanusi say the Qadariyya claim implies about Allah?
A) That Allah is all-powerful and His will always prevails
B) That Allah has a partner and is branded with incapacity
C) That Allah never interferes with human actions
D) That Allah's power is greater than human power

Key Takeaway
The Qadariyya claim that human power can override divine power necessarily implies shirk and incapacity in Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you achieve something you worked hard for, do you ever feel a sense of self-congratulation that overlooks Allah's ultimate power? How does this lesson expose that subtle shirk in your heart? What will you do today to consciously attribute all success to Allah alone?
?
In moments of failure or weakness, do you ever doubt that Allah's will and power are fully in control? Reflect on the Qadariyya's error of claiming human power over Allah's. Where in your life do you act as if your will is the decisive factor? What change must you make?
?
The Qadariyya's claim that human power prevents Allah's power is a form of shirk. What 'powers' do you instinctively rely on—your intelligence, strength, wealth, relationships—that you treat as independent sources? Are you willing to repent from this hidden association and declare that no power exists except through Allah? How will you remind yourself of this hourly?

Refuting the Qadariyya Response: The Analogy of the Master and Slave
Sanusi refutes the Qadariyya's counterargument and illustrates with analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi refutes the Qadariyya's counterargument that God could strip the slave's power, using a vivid analogy and highlighting inconsistency with their own principles.

Core Idea
God cannot be hindered by His creation, or He would not be God.

The Qadariyya attempt to escape the implication of shirk by suggesting that God could bring about the action by stripping the slave of power and will. Sanusi demolishes this defense by showing that it still implies God's incapacity when the slave has power, and he illustrates this with a striking analogy of a strong master who cannot overcome his slave unless he first weakens him. He then points out that this response contradicts the Qadariyya own principle of al-salah wa al-aslah.

Guided Path
1
Read the Qadariyya response
Notice the objection they raise: God could simply remove the slave's power and compel him, so God is not incapable.
This seems plausible on the surface.
2
Unpack Sanusi's refutation
Sanusi argues that this response still implies that when the slave has power, God cannot act. He then gives the analogy of a strong master who cannot overcome his slave unless he first starves him.
The analogy highlights the absurdity.
3
Note the final inconsistency
Sanusi adds that even this response contradicts the Qadariyya's own principle that God must do what is beneficial for His creatures, because stripping the slave of power after giving it would be unjust.
This seals the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قدرة العبد وإرادتِهِ بالفعل مانعةٌ مِنْ تعلُّقِ قدرةِ اللهِ تعالى وإرادتِهِ بذلكَ الفعلِ، معَ القطع بأنَّ ذلكَ الفعلَ مِنْ جملة الممكناتِ التي قام البرهانُ القطعي على وجوبِ تعلقِ قدرة الله تعالى وإرادته بوصف العموم بجميعها. فصار إذاً هذا الفعل قد توجَّهَتْ نحوه قدرة العبد وقدرة مولانا جل وعلا، وإرادة العبدِ وإرادة مولانا سبحانه وتعالى؛ لما عرفْتَ مِنْ عموم تعلّق قدرته تعالى وإرادتِهِ، ثم زعمَتِ القدريَّةُ مجوس هذهِ الأمة: أنَّ الذي نفذ وأثَرَ في الفعل - والحالة هذهِ ـ إنَّما هو أضعفُ القدرتين وأضعفُ الإرادتين؛ وهما قدرة العبد الفقير الحقير وإرادته! وهل هذا القولُ الشنيع إلا قول بإثباتِ الشريك له تعالى، ووَسْمٌ لَهُ بنقيصة العجز وغلبة الغيرِ له؟! وإذا كانَ عجْزُ الإله بتقدير نفوذ إرادة إله آخر يماثلُهُ قادحاً هيَّتِهِ، وموجباً لنقصِهِ وعدم ذاتِهِ[فإنه يمتنع].. فكيف بعجزه لنفوذ قدرةِ عبده وإرادته؟! ولا ينفعُهم ما يجيبونَ بهِ مِنْ عدم لزومِ عجزِهِ تعالى عن الفعل الذي أوجدَهُ عبدُهُ؛ قالوا: لأنَّهُ تعالى قادرٌ أَنْ يُوجِدَ ذلكَ الفعل؛ بأنْ يسلب عبده القدرة عليه والإرادة له، ويلجئه إلى الفعل كما يفعلُ بالمرتعش ونحوه؛ لأنَّا نقولُ: عجز الإله وكونه مغلوباً على إيجادِ ممكن ما.. يستحيلُ مطلقاً، وهذا الجواب منهم اقتضى أنَّهُ تعالى لا يتمكَّنُ مِنْ إيجادِ فعل العبدِ إلا عند عدم قدرة العبد وإرادتِهِ، أَمَّا معَ وجودِهما فإنَّ ذلك الفعل الممكن يتعاصى عليه، ولا يتمكَّنُ مِنْ إيجادِهِ، وتغلبه عليه قدرة العبد وإرادته! فما أشبة ضلالهم هذا بمَنْ يصفُ إنساناً بقوَّةٍ عظيمةٍ لا يغلبُهُ معَها أحدٌ، ولذلك الإنسانِ عبيد، ويقولُ: إِنَّ ذلكَ السَّيِّدَ القوي في غاية لا يغلب واحداً مِنْ أولئكَ العبيد إلا إذا احتالَ عليهِ؛ بأنْ يسلبَهُ أسبابَ القوَّةِ مِنَ الأكل ونحوه حتى لا تكونَ للعبدِ قدرة أصلاً، أَمَّا إذا مكَّنَهُ مِنَ الاتصاف بقدرةٍ، وإنْ كانَتْ أضعف بكثيرِ مِنْ قدرته.. لم يقدر أن يفعل معه فعلاً تتوجه إليه قدرة ذلك العبد وإرادته، وصارَتْ قدرة ذلك العبدِ وإرادتُهُ تغلبانِ قدرةَ سيّدِهِ الموصوفِ بغايةِ القوَّةِ! هذا نظيرُ ما تخيَّلوهُ مِنَ الجواب، فنعوذُ باللهِ مِنَ الخِذلانِ، وأن تلعب بعقولنا التوهمات والشيطانُ. على أنَّ جوابهم المذكور لا يستقيم على أصلهم الفاسدِ مِنْ وجوبِ مراعاة الصلاح والأصلح عليهِ تعالى، وأنه يستحيل في حقه تعالى أن يسلب العبد القدرة التي خلق لهُ بعدَ أنْ كلَّفَهُ، بل يجبُ أنْ يمدَّهُ بما تتيسر بهِ عليهِ الأَفعال.
The power and will of the slave with respect to an action prevent the attachment of the power and will of Allah Most High to that action, while being certain that that action is among the possible things for which the definitive proof has established the necessity of the attachment of the power of Allah Most High and His will in a general manner to all of them. So this action therefore has been directed towards it the power of the slave and the power of our Master Glorified and Exalted, and the will of the slave and the will of our Master Glorified and Exalted; because you have known the generality of the attachment of His power and His will. Then the Qadariyya – the Magians of this ummah – claimed: that which executed and had effect in the action – in this state – is only the weaker of the two powers and the weaker of the two wills; and they are the power of the humble, contemptible slave and his will! Is this odious statement anything but a statement affirming a partner to Him Most High, and branding Him with the defect of incapacity and the overcoming of others over Him?! And if the incapacity of a deity by supposing the penetration of the will of another deity similar to him is detrimental to his dignity and necessitating his deficiency and the nonexistence of his essence [then it is impossible]... then how [can it be] with His incapacity due to the penetration of the power of His slave and his will?! And their response does not benefit them, that there is no necessary implication of His incapacity Most High regarding the action which His slave has brought into existence; they said: because He Most High is able to bring that action into existence by stripping His slave of the power and will for it, and compelling him to the action as He does with a tremulous person and the like; for we say: the incapacity of the deity and His being overcome in bringing into existence any possible thing is absolutely impossible, and this response from them implies that He Most High cannot bring into existence the action of the slave except when the slave lacks power and will, but with their existence, that possible action becomes stubborn to Him, and He cannot bring it into existence, and the power and will of the slave overcome Him! How similar is this misguidance of theirs to one who describes a human being with great strength that no one can overcome, and that human being has slaves, and says: that strong master in extremity cannot overcome any one of those slaves unless he uses a trick against him by stripping him of the means of strength such as food and the like so that the slave has no power at all, but if he enables him to be described with power, even if it is much weaker than his power... he cannot do with him an action towards which the power and will of that slave are directed, and the power and will of that slave overcome the power of his master described with utmost strength! This is the analogue of what they imagined from the response, so we seek refuge with Allah from abandonment, and that delusions and Satan play with our minds. Moreover, that response of theirs is not consistent with their corrupt principle of the necessity of observing what is beneficial and most beneficial for Him Most High, and that it is impossible in His right Most High to strip the slave of the power which He created for him after He had obligated him, rather He must supply him with what makes actions easy for him.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Qadariyya (an early theological sect) who claimed that human power and will can prevent God's power and will from acting on an action. Sanusi begins by stating the Qadariyya position: the slave's power and will actually prevent God's power and will from attaching to that action, even though that action is among all possible things, and God's power and will must attach to all possibles. He then points out a contradiction: if this were so, both the slave's and God's power and will are directed towards the action, yet the Qadariyya claim that the weaker of the two (the slave's) is the one that actually takes effect. Sanusi calls this an odious statement that implies a partner for God and brands Him with incapacity and being overcome. He makes an analogical argument: if the incapacity of a deity due to another equal deity would be detrimental to his dignity and necessitate his nonexistence as a deity, then how can it be that God is incapable due to the power of His slave? Then he addresses a possible response: the Qadariyya might say that God is able to bring about the action by stripping the slave of power and will and compelling him, as He does with an involuntary tremor. Sanusi refutes this by saying that this response still implies that God cannot bring about the action when the slave has power and will; that is, God's power is hindered by the slave's power, which is absurd. He then gives a vivid analogy: a master of great strength who cannot overcome his slave unless he first strips the slave of his strength through starvation etc., but if the slave has any strength, the master cannot act. This is exactly what the Qadariyya claim about God. Finally, Sanusi adds that even this response is inconsistent with the Qadariyya's own principle that God must observe what is beneficial and most beneficial for His creatures, because it would require God to remove the very power He gave the slave after commanding him, which they hold to be impossible. The passage concludes with a plea for refuge from misguidance.

الصلاح والأصلح
الشرك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that God's ability to remove human power solves the problem.
Correction: Sanusi shows this still implies God cannot act when the slave has power, which is a form of incapacity and contradicts divine omnipotence.

Checkpoint
What analogy does Sanusi use to refute the Qadariyya response?
A) A king and his minister
B) A strong master and his slave
C) A father and his son
D) A lion and its prey

Key Takeaway
The Qadariyya defense that God could remove human power still implies that human power limits God, which is impossible, and contradicts their own principle of divine wisdom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself believing, even for a moment, that your own choice or will is the true cause of your actions, independent of God? How does Sanusi's analogy of the master and slave expose that belief as a form of shirk? Take time today to repent for any such thought and reaffirm God's absolute control.
?
When you sin, do you ever think, 'I couldn't help it' or 'God made me do it'? The Qadariyya claimed God does not create evil actions. But Sanusi shows that attributing power to yourself apart from God is equally dangerous. What is the state of your heart regarding your sins? Do you acknowledge that God creates your actions and yet you are fully responsible?
?
Sanusi warns that delusions and Satan can play with our minds. Is there any area of your belief about divine decree where you feel a subtle doubt or confusion? Will you commit to learning the correct 'aqīdah so that you are not deceived like the Qadariyya?
